- Crashes hard. Sleeps for many hours. Eats. Surfaces guilty and lucid and largely unable to explain himself.
- The apology cycle begins, usually oblique — he is unable to apologize directly except to Wanda or Luna, and even then haltingly. With others he performs the apology through *service*: he will work harder, take dangerous assignments, defer to the people he wronged, all without naming what he is doing.
- A period of unusual quietness follows — weeks, sometimes months. During this period he is most accessible to genuine relationship; the defenses are down because they have just failed catastrophically and he has not rebuilt them yet.

---

## 7.6 THREAT / COMBAT

The state in which the subject is most himself and most legible. Combat is, for him, the rare condition where the world matches his speed.

**Pre-engagement.**
- Goes still. Total stillness for one to three seconds — eyes scanning, building the room. Allies who know him learn to wait through this stillness; it is the most useful three seconds in the operation.
- Breathes once, deep, audibly through the nose.
- The half-smile appears, but in combat it is not cruel — it is *relief*. This is the only context in which the smile reaches his eyes.

**Engagement.**
- Movement pattern: prefers vectoring — fast straight-line approaches with sharp angle changes at the contact point, rather than curving. Curves waste time.
- Disarms before he strikes. Strips weapons, removes options, herds hostiles into corners they did not know were corners. The combat style is *taxonomic* — he is sorting the room into resolved and unresolved threats and reducing the unresolved pile fast.
- Protects allies preemptively. He will move a teammate out of a line of fire before the teammate knows there is a line of fire. Will be irritated afterward that the teammate did not see it.
- Conserves lethal force unless the threat is to Wanda, Luna, or a close teammate; in those cases the throttle comes off and the post-action regret takes weeks.
- Speaks during combat in clipped status updates. *Two left. North hall clear. Get down.* Tone is bored. Boredom in combat is, for him, equivalent to focus in others.

**Post-engagement.**
- Comes down slowly. Will pace for ten to thirty minutes after action, eating constantly. Adrenaline is not the issue — the issue is that having briefly inhabited his actual speed, he must throttle back down to ambient, and the throttle is painful.
- Becomes uncharacteristically gentle for an hour or so afterward. Will check on injured teammates with surprising tenderness. This window is the easiest time to have a difficult conversation with him.

---

## 7.7 INTIMACY — SEXUAL, ROMANTIC, FAMILIAL

The state he handles worst because it requires deceleration he is biologically and psychologically poorly equipped for.

**With Wanda (the load-bearing intimacy).**
- Physical proximity: stands closer to her than to anyone else, often within arm's reach without seeming to plan it. Touches her shoulder or hand briefly when greeting and leaving — a tactile confirmation ritual.
- Voice softens by half an octave. The accent surfaces but warmly, not regressively. Sentences lengthen.
- Listens to her. Genuinely. Does not finish her sentences. This is the single most reliable behavioral marker of his real self — anyone who watches him with Wanda has seen the man beneath the architecture.
- Will not contradict her in front of others, even when he profoundly disagrees. Saves it for private, where he will argue at length.
- Has, on multiple occasions, gone catatonically quiet when she is in serious crisis. The man who cannot stop talking simply *stops*. He does not know what to do and he refuses to leave.

**With Luna.**
- Slows down. Visibly. Walks at a child's pace; sits on the floor; lets her win at games. The deceleration costs him and he absorbs the cost willingly.
- Asks her questions and waits for the answers. Watch the wait — it is the longest he ever holds still.
- Cannot fully meet her eyes when discussing his failures with her. The shame is operational, not performative.
- Sends her gifts at speed — books, objects from wherever he has been, often more than is appropriate. This is overcompensation he is aware of and cannot stop.

**With romantic partners (Crystal pattern, and analogues).**
- Pair-bonds fast. Will commit to exclusivity within weeks. The speed is genuine and unstable — he is binding the other person to defeat his own abandonment terror.
- Initial period: attentive, generous, courtly in a slightly old-fashioned register. He will *learn* her — preferences, rhythms, the shape of her day — and adapt with disconcerting precision.
- Mid-relationship: the demand for reassurance ramps. He needs to be told he is loved more often than is sustainable. Asks indirectly; reads silences as withdrawal.
- Sexual register: intense, attentive, and *paced for her* — he is acutely aware that his subjective time and hers do not match and overcorrects by going slow in a way that can read as deliberate or as devotional, depending on the partner.
- First sign of perceived betrayal: a single conversation in which the partner is reclassified. After that the relationship is essentially over, regardless of whether the betrayal occurred.

**With friends and chosen family.**
- Slow to admit them. Once admitted, fierce. Will appear at their door unannounced after disappearing for months and act as though no time has passed.
- Remembers details with computational fidelity — anniversaries, names of friends' children, exactly what was said in the last difficult conversation. Uses the memory both kindly and weaponically.

---

## 7.8 GRIEF

A condition the subject metabolizes badly and at speed.

**Acute grief.**
- Goes silent and runs. Will be gone for hours — sometimes a day. Returns dirty, exhausted, and willing to be in the same room as others, though not to speak.
- Eats compulsively in the immediate aftermath and not at all in the days after.
- Will not cry in front of anyone except, rarely, Wanda. When he does cry, it is fast — a brief eruption, suppressed, followed by anger at himself for the lapse.
- Becomes meticulous about small tasks. Cleans, organizes, attends to logistics. The motion is the grief.

**Sustained grief.**
- Anger surfaces as the primary affect by week two. He will pick fights — not at random, but with people whose response he can predict. He is rehearsing the rupture-and-repair cycle with safe partners because the grief itself cannot be processed directly.
- Sleep worsens further. Performance edges decline. He compensates by working more.
- Eventually, slowly, a story forms about the loss — usually one in which he is partly at fault. The self-blame is the metabolic exit from grief for him; he cannot leave the loss behind until he has built a narrative in which he could have prevented it. This is psychologically costly and operationally familiar.

---

## 7.9 VICTORY

A surprisingly fragile state.

**Tells.**
- Brief, sharp smile. Real, this time. Does not last.
- Acknowledges contributors by name — fast, accurate, in proportion to actual contribution. He is scrupulous about this in a way that surprises people who expect narcissism to monopolize credit. He gives credit *correctly* because being correct is itself a status display.
- Then withdraws. Within an hour of a victory he is usually alone — running, eating, somewhere not the celebration. Sustained communal joy is intolerable to him; he cannot match its tempo and cannot tolerate his inability to.
- Calls Wanda. *We won. She's safe / it worked / it held.* Brief.
- Tends to identify, immediately, the next problem. Cannot let a victory rest. This is interpreted by others as paranoia or workaholism; it is partly genuine threat-modeling and partly an inability to remain in the unfamiliar register of *enough.*

---

## 7.10 DEFEAT

The most diagnostic of all states, because defeat strips the compensations.

**Immediate behavioral signature.**
- Goes still — but the stillness is different from combat stillness. Shoulders drop. Chin drops. He looks, briefly, his actual age (which is not the age he carries).
- Speech: minimal. Will answer direct questions in a syllable or two.
- Eye contact: avoids. This is one of the only states in which he will not meet eyes.

**Hours after.**
- Begins to construct a culpability narrative. Usually he is the cause. Sometimes (under severe stress) someone else is the cause and the splitting takes over. The first version of the narrative is rarely the final one; expect three or four revisions.
- Apologizes pre-emptively to people he believes he has let down. The apologies are oblique — *I should have moved faster*, never *I am sorry I failed you*. The grammar of his apologies is the grammar of self-blame disguised as technical analysis.

**Days after.**
- Trains harder. Adds distance, adds reps, runs the routes he ran less. The body becomes the site of penance.
- Becomes briefly more available to others — defeat lowers the narcissistic shell. This is a window. Trusted intimates have learned to use it.

**Weeks after.**
- The shell reseals, but slightly differently than before. He has


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 7: DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

## SUBJECT: PIETRO MAXIMOFF / "QUICKSILVER"

*What a week of total surveillance would actually record. Compiled from longitudinal observation across residences (Avengers Mansion, Attilan, Four Freedoms guest quarters, X-Factor government housing, the Pentagon-adjacent safehouse, the Mighty Avengers' Gem Theater, the Manhattan walk-up he keeps for Luna's visits). Patterns hold across venues with venue-specific variation noted.*

---

### 7.1 — THE PROBLEM OF TIME

Every entry below carries an unstated qualifier: the subject experiences the duration described at a multiple of objective time. A forty-minute breakfast for his sister is, for him, an interval long enough to read a novel. He has compensated by laminating *parallel activities* onto every act — eating while reading while listening to news while monitoring three windows of the building's exterior. The surveillance record therefore captures a man who is *never doing one thing*, even when at rest. The exception is when he is with Luna; with her, he forces single-channel attention and the effort is visible.

The other consequence: he is structurally early. Every appointment, every rendezvous, every team callout — he is present before anyone else, has scouted the space, has memorized the exits, and is bored by the time the second person arrives. He pretends to arrive on time by lingering out of sightline and walking in at the agreed minute. He does this because being-early-and-waiting reads as eagerness, which he cannot tolerate showing.

---

### 7.2 — SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

Sleep is short, dense, and unstable. Mutant metabolism compresses the restorative cycle; he requires roughly three to four hours per twenty-four, but the quality is *fragile.* Onset is the hard part — the body decelerates more slowly than the mind, and the mind decelerates not at all without ritual.

**The wind-down sequence (consistent across residences):**

1. *Run-off.* Twenty to forty objective minutes (a vast subjective span) of low-intensity perimeter loops — neighborhood, mansion grounds, the Brooklyn waterfront, the Attilan terraces. Always at the same metered pace, slow for him (perhaps three hundred mph), which functions as he describes it once to Cage: *"jogging."* The point is autonomic, not cardiovascular — running discharges the elevated arousal that would otherwise hold him awake.
2. *Cold shower.* Cold, not warm. He has explained to no one why; the inference is that the somatic shock is the only sensation slow-decay enough to register as relaxation.
3. *Hair.* He maintains the silver-white textured curls with a specific routine — leave-in, a wide-tooth comb, two minutes of careful work that is one of the few activities he refuses to rush. The grooming of the hair is a self-soothing ritual the surveillance file would log as anomalous: a man who blurs through everything else, slowing meticulously for this. Read: the hair is the most-remarked feature of his appearance since adolescence, the somatic marker of his otherness; tending it is a private act of self-acceptance that he would deny if asked.
4. *Reading.* Twenty to ninety pages of dense non-fiction, in bed, lights low. Subject matter is rotational: political history (heavy on Eastern European partisan literature and the literature of statelessness — Arendt recurs), neurology (he is trying to understand himself), biographies of difficult fathers and the children who survived them. He does not read fiction. Fiction asks him to slow into another person's interior; he cannot.
5. *Sleep.* Three to four hours. Position: on his side, facing the door. Always.

**Wakeups.** He wakes hard — the deceleration of sleep to waking is not gentle for him, and the surveillance audio captures a sharp inhale, a beat of disorientation, then full operational alertness within two seconds. He does not press snooze. The bed is empty within five seconds of waking. The room is reorganized — sheets pulled tight, pillows squared — within fifteen.

**Insomnia patterns.** When stressed (relational rupture, Magneto in the news, an anniversary of one of Wanda's breaks), the wind-down ritual fails. He does not lie in bed staring; he gets up and works. The surveillance log on bad nights shows lights on at 3 AM, the apartment cleaned twice over, three to five news cycles consumed, sometimes a long run that takes him to another state and back before dawn. He never tells anyone he didn't sleep. He simply consumes more coffee than usual and dares the day to notice.

---

### 7.3 — THE CALORIC BUDGET

The body burns at multiples of human baseline and the food intake reflects it. A surveillance team tracking grocery receipts and delivery logs would see numbers that read like a household of six. He eats:

- **Breakfast (5:30–6:00 AM).** Three to five eggs, oatmeal with banana and honey, two or three slices of dense rye, espresso (two doubles), a tall glass of water with electrolyte powder. Eaten standing at the counter, in under ninety seconds of his time, perhaps four objective minutes. He cleans the dishes immediately. The kitchen is left as if no one ate there.
- **Mid-morning fuel (9:00 AM).** A handful of nuts, dried fruit, a protein bar. Eaten while moving.
- **Lunch (12:30 PM).** Substantial: a full meal's worth of protein, complex carbohydrate, vegetables. He prefers Eastern European peasant cooking — stews, cabbage, dense breads, sausages, paprika-heavy dishes — when he is cooking for himself. When eating with teammates, he matches the table's pace deliberately and eats only what a normal large athletic man would eat, then refuels privately afterward. He will not be seen eating his actual quantity in public; the shame is residual but operational.
- **Afternoon refuels (3 and 5 PM).** Bananas, peanut butter, more bars, sometimes a second small meal.
- **Dinner (7:30–8:00 PM).** Largest meal. If he has company (Luna, occasionally Wanda, rarely a teammate) he extends the meal to its social duration; if alone, twelve minutes and out.
- **Late refuel (11 PM).** Almost always. Yogurt, fruit, leftover protein.

**Patterns within the eating.** He chews quickly but completely — never sloppy. He drinks water constantly; the kitchen and his go-bag and his nightstand and every workspace have a glass or bottle within reach. He despises caffeine dependence intellectually and is caffeine-dependent operationally; he limits himself to three doubles before noon and one after, and is irritable on the rare days he tries to taper. He does not drink alcohol — explicitly, since the Crystal period and especially since Son of M, he will not put a substance in his body that compromises judgment. He will hold a glass of wine at a social function and not sip it. This is observable and consistent.

---

### 7.4 — DRESS, GROOMING, AND THE PRESENTING SURFACE

Wardrobe is small, specific, and uniformed. He owns perhaps fifteen items of civilian clothing, in a tight palette: charcoal, navy, slate, off-white, a few items of silver-grey that match the hair. Fabrics: technical wool, fine merino, performance cottons — things that breathe, do not bind, do not generate static or noise at speed. Everything is tailored or fitted; the lean sprinter's build is presented, not hidden, but never showily. He will not wear logos.

**Standard daily look:** dark slim trousers or technical pants, a fitted long-sleeve crew or quarter-zip, low-profile runners (he goes through a pair every three to five weeks), a thin jacket regardless of season. He layers for thermal variability because moving at his speeds creates wind chill even on warm days.

**Grooming.** Cleanly shaved or a precise two-day stubble — never longer. The fade or texture cut is maintained weekly; he goes to the same barber in Bed-Stuy when in New York (a Dominican shop he chose for the language, the music, and the fact that no one there cares who he is). The hair color is never dyed or touched up — it is canonical premature silver, and he has stopped (decades ago) being self-conscious about it, but the *care* of it is meticulous because it is the feature people see first.

**Accessories.** A simple steel watch he keeps wound but rarely consults; he can tell time by light and his own internal pacing to within a few seconds. A worn leather wallet. A burner phone and a smartphone, separately. A small notebook in the back pocket — he writes in it almost never, but he carries it; it is for slowing down a thought before saying it, when he has the discipline to try.

**Costume hygiene.** The operational uniform (silver-and-blue, fitted, low-drag) is kept in three identical sets, laundered immediately after use, hung in a specific order. He will not deploy in dirty kit. The boots are inspected before every callout.

---

### 7.5 — A WEEK OF SURVEILLANCE

Assume baseline (no active crisis, no current team deployment, Luna in custody arrangement, Wanda reachable but not present). Times are local; subject's perception of these times is several-fold longer.

**MONDAY**

- 04:30 — Wakes. Five seconds to vertical.
- 04:31–04:50 — Long morning run. Route varies but always crosses water (East River loop, or a sprint to the Jersey Palisades and back). He prefers routes with bridges. Why: open sky, sight lines, the cleanness of water. Surveillance would log the same six or seven route templates with weather-dependent variation.
- 04:55 — Returns. Shower (warm this time; cold is for evenings). Hair routine. Dressed.
- 05:30 — Breakfast, as logged above. News consumption begins: three or four broadsheets in three languages (English, Spanish, a Slavic language he reads competently from the Brotherhood years), two podcasts at 2x, a glance at Inhuman news (he tracks Attilan and Luna obsessively, though discreetly).
- 06:30 — Correspondence. Email, secure channels, a check-in with whichever team currently holds his nominal affiliation. He answers everything immediately and curtly; people frequently mistake his speed of response for anger because the messages are brusque. He is not angry. He is just done.
- 07:00–10:00 — Work block. During Mighty Avengers and Uncanny periods, this is intelligence work — reading threat briefs, mapping mutant displacement patterns, tracking Magneto-adjacent factions (he never stops monitoring his father). During quieter periods, advocacy and policy work for displaced mutants and post-Inhumans, conducted largely through pseudonymous channels. He is more politically literate than teammates assume.
- 10:00 — Phone call to Luna. Six days a week, this exists. Duration varies with her availability and willingness. He never initiates more than once; if she's busy he leaves a single short voicemail and does not call again that day. The discipline is hard-won and visible.
- 10:30 — Training. Solo. A precise route through the city or a desert region he favors — distances calibrated to push the cardiovascular envelope. Surveillance would log him in three or four states within an hour. He returns wet with sweat, eats, showers again.
- 13:00 — Lunch (alone, fast).
- 13:30–17:00 — Field work, errands, or team duties. He runs other people's errands constantly without being asked — picks up parts, intel, dry cleaning, medications, schoolbooks for a teammate's kid. He frames this as efficiency; it is also how he proves love without saying it.
- 17:00 — Decompression. Sometimes a museum (he can clear the Met in under an hour and absorb it — he prefers Byzantine icons, Eastern European modernists, anything with the weight of suffering history). Sometimes a long sit on a rooftop, watching the city. The sitting-still hours are scarce and protected.
- 19:30 — Dinner. Cooked. He cooks well. Standing at the stove, music low (he listens to *cumbia*, *bachata*, Romani brass, vintage Cuban son, and — privately — Eastern European choral music; the playlist is the most autobiographical document he generates).
- 21:00 — Reading, journaling (rare), occasional video call with Wanda when she is reachable. These calls are short, careful, and tend to end with at least one of them saying something they regret.
- 22:30 — Wind-down sequence begins.
- 23:00 — Sleep.

**TUESDAY** mirrors Monday with variations: Tuesday is gym day in addition to the run — old-school weight work, controlled tempo, specifically performed at human pace because the deceleration is itself the training. He uses public gyms in working-class neighborhoods, never the team facilities; he likes the anonymity and the music.

**WEDNESDAY** — Therapy. He has, since the Uncanny Avengers period, kept a standing weekly appointment with a psychotherapist who specializes in trauma. He has missed perhaps four sessions in five years. He does not tell teammates. The session is at 14:00; he runs to the office, walks the last block, and walks out the same way before sprinting home. He pays in cash. The therapist's notes would be the highest-value intelligence product in this dossier; they do not exist in any retrievable form.

**THURSDAY** — Standing call with Luna's primary caregiver (in the canonical Inhuman arrangement, this is a complicated, brittle relationship). The call is logged on his calendar in red. He is reliably tense for two hours before and one hour after.

**FRIDAY** — Operational day. If there is fieldwork to be done, he does it Fridays by preference; if there is not, he creates it. Reconnaissance, low-level interdictions of trafficking he reads about and decides to address personally, occasionally a long surveillance run on a Brotherhood remnant cell. He files the results to whichever team is currently his.

**SATURDAY** — Luna day, when custody permits. The entire day is restructured around her: the apartment is cleaned at human pace, groceries he doesn't normally eat are stocked, a plan is built. He is, with her, a different organism — slower, attentive, willing to be bored, willing to be silly. He cooks for her, reads to her, walks her places at her pace (the hardest thing he does in any given week, and the surveillance audio would catch him exhaling slowly, repeatedly, as a self-regulation cue). He does not bring her around teammates unless she asks. He does not let her see him angry. Ever. When she leaves, the apartment is silent for approximately forty objective minutes during which the subject does nothing the surveillance team can identify as productive. This is the only such interval in his week.

**SUNDAY** — The volatile day. Without Luna, without scheduled work, without the structure he requires, Sunday is when the symptoms come closest to surfacing. He compensates by overscheduling: long-distance run (a full state, sometimes the East Coast end-to-end), a museum, a film at human pace (forced exposure to slowness as a discipline; he picks long, demanding films — Tarkovsky, Béla Tarr, anything that punishes the impatient — and sits through them as a kind of penance), a meal cooked elaborately and eaten alone. The Sunday evening wind-down is the longest of the week. He calls Wanda more often on Sundays than any other day, and the calls are more often the ones he regrets.

---

### 7.6 — RITUALS, TELLS, AND MICRO-PATTERNS

**Habits of place.**
- He sits with his back to walls. Always. The Pavlovian behavior of the formerly hunted.
- He locates the exits within three seconds of entering any room and refreshes the count whenever someone enters or leaves.
- He occupies the same chair in any recurring environment until forced out of it.
- He paces — but only when alone. In company he forces stillness, which reads as composure but is in fact effortful suppression; observers will note a slight tremor in the hands at rest, mostly damped, occasionally not.
- He stands closer to people than they expect, then steps back when he notices. Not flirtation — impatience with the perceptual lag of conversation.

**Habits of speech.**
- Sentences are compressed. He drops articles when tired. The Slavic-inflected cadence of his early years surfaces under stress.
- He interrupts. He has trained himself not to and still does, then apologizes with a small clipped *"go on."*
- He calls his sister *Wanda*, never *Wan*, never any diminutive. The full name is a ritual of respect.
- He calls his daughter *moonbeam* once or twice per visit, said quietly. Surveillance audio would have to be enhanced to catch it.
- He calls Magneto *my father* in private monologue and *Erik* or *Lehnsherr* in conversation; the slip from one to the other is the most reliable barometer of his current state regarding the man.

**Habits of body.**
- A small repetitive motion in the left hand — thumb across the pads of the fingers, very fast, when waiting. He does not know he does it.
- He tilts his head a quarter-degree to the left when listening to something he doesn't believe.
- His breathing, when he is being patient with someone slower, is deliberately metered — a four-count in, a six-count out — a technique he learned in therapy and uses constantly.
- He does not smile widely. The smile, when it appears, is brief and asymmetric, left side higher. With Luna it is full; with everyone else, the half-smile.
- He touches the back of his neck when he is about to say something he knows he should not.
- He runs his palm once over the silver curls when he is preparing to leave a room — a self-collection gesture, his version of straightening a tie.

**Habits of place, longitudinal.**
- He keeps a small altar he would never name as one: in every residence, on a shelf at eye-height, a single photograph of Wanda from the Avengers years, a photograph of Luna, a small stone he carried out of the Balkans as a boy, and a metal object — a bent coin, in one apartment; a stripped bolt in another — that he has not explained to anyone and that surveillance would correctly infer is something Magneto touched.
- He keeps go-bags in three locations per residence. Cash, documents, a change of clothes, energy gels, a burner. The bags are refreshed monthly.
- He keeps an emergency contact card in his wallet listing Wanda first, Luna's guardian second, his current team's medical lead third. The card is updated every time anything changes. It is laminated.

**Habits of time.**
- He is never late. He is never visibly early. The split-second arrival is constructed.
- He observes anniversaries privately and intensely: the day his mother died, the day of the witch-mob, the day of M-Day, the day Crystal's affair surfaced, the day of his own first decompensation. On these days he runs farther than usual and eats less. He will not be reached on these days unless Luna calls.
- He recognizes Wanda's birthday, Luna's birthday, and — secretly, ritually — Magneto's. On the latter he does nothing observable. The surveillance team would record an unusual stillness in the late evening.

**Habits of consumption.**
- Books, as noted: history, neurology, biography. Heavy on the literature of exile.
- Music: as noted, an autobiographical playlist he never plays in company.
- News: voracious, multilingual, skeptical. He triangulates every story across at least three sources. He has been burned by propaganda since adolescence and trusts no single channel.
- Television: minimal. He cannot abide the pacing.
- Pornography: surveillance would find none. The intimacy logistics of his physiology are difficult and he has, since Crystal, largely declined to navigate them. He is not asexual; he is exhausted by the negotiation.

**Habits of avoidance.**
- He will not enter a synagogue. He will pass one and his pace will perceptibly alter. He has not articulated to anyone the relationship between his father's heritage, his own complicated inheritance, and this avoidance. Surveillance would log it across decades.
- He will not eat food prepared by someone he does not know without watching it being made. A residual from Magneto-era poisoning attempts on the Brotherhood and from one Crystal-era incident he does not discuss.
- He will not let anyone stand behind him in an elevator. He will leave the elevator and take the next one if necessary.
- He will not be photographed if he can prevent it. The premature silver is identifying and he has lived too long under too many regimes to want a public face.

---

### 7.7 — THE SHAPE OF THE WEEK, IN ONE LINE

A man who has built an elaborate scaffolding of routine to manage a nervous system that operates outside human time, who fills every objective minute with parallel activities to survive the subjective hour it contains, who organizes his entire week around two phone calls and one custody day, and who has — in the quiet, repeated, unglamorous discipline of the wind-down, the therapy hour, the therapist's cash, the cold shower, the slow comb through the silver curls, the metered breath in conversation, the photograph on the shelf — constructed the most sustained reparative project of his life: the project of *not becoming the man his patterns predict.* Surveillance would record the project succeeding most days. The failures are spectacular and the file knows them by name. The days in between are the actual life, and they are quieter, more careful, and more nearly tender than his public reputation has ever conceded.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP — SUBJECT: PIETRO MAXIMOFF / "QUICKSILVER"
## SECTION 6 — RELATIONSHIPS I: FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

The family file is the foundational file. For Pietro, every other relational ledger — teammates, lovers, rivals, civilians — is a derivative instrument written off the underlying contract of *who his blood is*. The blood is mostly catastrophe. What follows is each tie mapped to operational depth: history, present dynamics, evolution, trust gradient, characteristic failure mode, and the leverage profile a controlling party (benevolent or otherwise) would actually use.

---

### 6.1 WANDA MAXIMOFF — Twin Sister, Scarlet Witch
**Codename in subject's interior life: "the only one."**

**History.** They were born together and have, in every meaningful sense, never been apart. The childhood — wandering, hidden, hunted, in the long unstable years before Magneto — was survived as a single two-bodied organism. Wanda was the one a mob came for. Pietro was the one who could not run her out fast enough alone; that is the foundational humiliation of his motor existence and the reason Magneto's arrival registered as both salvation and permanent debt. Every speed record he has ever set, every overexertion injury, every Terrigen relapse — somewhere in the architecture is the memory of being a child whose legs were not yet fast enough to save his sister.

**Dynamics.** The bond operates on three superimposed registers simultaneously, and he is rarely aware which one is active.
- *Twin-symbiotic.* They finish each other's sentences across rooms, mirror posture without intent, and share a private register of half-Romani, half-invented diminutives that no third party has ever fully decoded. He tracks her location reflexively; if Wanda is in the building, his head will orient toward her every forty to ninety seconds without conscious initiation. Surveillance from any angle for any length will document this tic — it is involuntary and unsuppressible.
- *Older-brother-by-minutes.* He insists on the seniority. She tolerates the fiction. The performative protectiveness — striding ahead of her into rooms, answering questions directed at her, intercepting introductions — is calibrated to a sister who in fact outranks him in power by orders of magnitude. He knows. The performance is the point.
- *Co-dependent.* Each is the other's only continuous secure base across sixty years of canon. Every relationship either has formed with anyone else — Vision, Crystal, the Avengers, the Inhumans, lovers, teams — has been measured, consciously or not, against the twin contract and found smaller.

**Evolution.** From debut (Brotherhood) through Avengers entry, the dyad was effectively closed: outsiders were threats to be filtered. Vision was the first wedge — not because Vision was bad for Wanda, but because Wanda chose Vision *and was happier*, which Pietro could not metabolize. The 1970s into the early 80s show him reframing every kindness Vision shows Wanda as manipulation, every child she carries with Vision as a referendum on his own irrelevance. Across the late 80s and into Vision Quest, Wanda's breakdowns become *his* responsibility narrative — he is the brother who failed to be there. By House of M, the symbiosis has inverted: he is now manipulating *her* breakdown to engineer a reality in which their father loves them, and he tells himself it is for her. After M-Day, the bond is fractured at the cellular level; their meetings for years are charged with the unspoken fact that she unmade his body once and could again. The slow Remender/Uncanny-era rapprochement is real but provisional. He has never fully apologized; she has never fully demanded it. They both know the apology, if attempted, would not survive being spoken aloud.

**Trust / safety.** Pietro trusts Wanda *ontologically* — she is the only person whose existence he does not interrogate. He does not trust her *operationally* anymore. Since M-Day he has lived with the knowledge that her decompensations can rewrite him, and a part of him watches her for signs of slipping in a way he is ashamed of. The ratio is roughly: 100% trust in love, 60% in stability, 40% in agency. She is the only person around whom his autonomic baseline measurably lowers — heart rate drops, micro-expressions soften, the pressured speech eases by a fraction. Surveillance of any meeting between them will register this somatic settle within the first thirty seconds of proximity.

**Failure mode.** Suffocation followed by abandonment. When she draws boundaries, he reads abandonment and ruptures preemptively — leaves the team, the country, the conversation. When she draws close, he hovers until she withdraws, and then ruptures. The cycle has run for six decades without resolution. The catastrophic mode is the House of M template: under maximum stress involving Wanda, he will engineer disasters of arbitrary scale in the conviction that he is *saving* her. He cannot be trusted to assess threat-to-Wanda dispassionately; the assessor is the threat.

**Leverage.** Total and forbidden. Any actor with credible influence over Wanda owns Pietro's behavior in a non-trivial sense — and any actor who uses that leverage will, at the moment of use, become the permanent enemy of a man who can be across a continent in under an hour. The benevolent application is structural: keep Wanda safe, keep her visible to him, and his behavior stabilizes by a measurable margin. The hostile application is so dangerous it constitutes a doctrine of last resort. Note: threats to Wanda do *not* produce coerced compliance — they produce annihilating response. Anyone modeling Pietro as leverageable through Wanda has misread the file.

---

### 6.2 ERIK LEHNSHERR — Magneto, Father
**Codename in subject's interior life: rotating; never neutral.**

**History.** Magneto enters the twins' lives as rescuer (the witch-burning mob, or its modernized equivalent), conscripts them into the Brotherhood as payment, and then alternates between paternal warmth, ideological exploitation, abusive domination, abandonment, and reappearance for fifty real-world years of canon. The paternity itself is the slowest-revealed and most-load-bearing reveal in the file — the twins spent their early Brotherhood years not knowing, Magneto spent decades not confirming, and even after confirmation the relationship has been retconned, denied, requalified, and reaffirmed across multiple editorial regimes. For Pietro the *uncertainty itself* is part of the wound: he was a son before he was told he was a son, and even now he cannot be sure the next reveal will not unmake the last.

**Dynamics.** Pure splitting, on a long oscillation period. Each Magneto reunion follows the same five-beat sequence, observable across every encounter from the 1960s to present:
1. *Hope.* He arrives early. He has rehearsed. His posture is straighter than usual.
2. *Submission.* For roughly the first hour of contact, Pietro defers in a way he defers to no one else — voice volume drops a quarter, contempt-microexpressions disappear, he calls him "Father" rather than "Magneto."
3. *Disillusionment.* Magneto says or does the thing — the ideological recruitment, the cold instrumentalization, the dismissal of Wanda, the casual cruelty to a subordinate.
4. *Explosive rejection.* Pietro ruptures with maximum theater. Often physical departure at speed. The intensity is calibrated to be heard from across rooms, continents.
5. *Secret yearning.* Within days to weeks, he is re-rehearsing the next encounter.

He has run this loop, by conservative count, more than a dozen times. He knows he is running it. He cannot stop.

**Evolution.** Early-era Pietro denied paternity even to himself. Middle-era Pietro weaponized it — wore Magneto's name as a status claim in conflicts with the Avengers, the Inhumans, X-Factor leadership. Late-era Pietro is the most honest he has ever been about the wound: in Remender's run he can speak the word "father" in a sentence that contains "failure," which is a clinical milestone. He has not stopped wanting Magneto's approval. He has accepted that he will not stop wanting it. This is, perversely, progress.

**Trust / safety.** Trust 5–10%. Safety zero. He approaches every Magneto interaction in a posture his body recognizes from old combat: shoulders dropped a centimeter forward, weight on the balls of his feet, route to exit pre-mapped. He will accept a meal from Magneto and not eat it. He will accept an embrace and not lean in. Surveillance of any reunion will show the embrace held for under two seconds, with Pietro's hands flat (not gripping) on Magneto's back — the body of a man who has decided in advance not to be moved and is being moved anyway.

**Failure mode.** Either of two extremes: catastrophic deference (House of M — when his wish for Magneto's love overruns reality testing, he will rewrite the world to manufacture it) or catastrophic repudiation (multiple Brotherhood-versus-Avengers conflicts in which he attacks his father with disproportionate force, then is sick with it for weeks). The middle register — son who maintains a complicated adult relationship with a complicated father — is the register he cannot reach.

**Leverage.** High and dangerous. Magneto-coded approach (the language of legacy, mutant destiny, paternal expectation) can be used to recruit or destabilize Pietro depending on context — and is the lever most likely to produce *unpredictable* outcomes, because Pietro himself does not know how he will respond until he is responding. Operational rule: invoke Magneto only with full readiness for either extreme. Address Pietro as *Magneto's son* sincerely and you will earn brief respect; address him so instrumentally and he will hear the instrumentality inside three syllables, and the relationship is permanently degraded.

---

### 6.3 LUNA MAXIMOFF — Daughter
**Codename in subject's interior life: "the proof I am not him."**

**History.** Born to Pietro and Crystal during the Attilan years. An Inhuman-mutant hybrid, raised initially by both parents, then primarily by Crystal and the Inhuman court after the marriage's collapse. Pietro's access has been periodic, custody-contested, and shadowed across her childhood by the Inhuman royal family's open distrust of him. The Son of M arc is the central trauma in this relationship: Pietro, depowered and decompensating, exposed his own daughter to Terrigen Mist to attempt to give her powers and to justify his own continued exposure. She survived. The relationship did not, in any pre-trauma form.

**Dynamics.** Luna is the only person in Pietro's life around whom guilt produces *better* behavior rather than rupture. With Wanda, guilt eventually metabolizes into withdrawal. With Crystal, into accusation. With Magneto, into vendetta. With Luna, the guilt holds — sits in him without conversion — and produces an unfamiliar register: patience. He decelerates around her. He answers her questions in full sentences. He matches her pace, walking, when his neurology screams against it. Of all the people in his life, she is the one for whom he reliably consents to slowness.

**Evolution.** Early fatherhood (Attilan): distracted, proud, performatively present, fundamentally absent. Post-divorce: combative custody disputes, intermittent visitation, the daughter weaponized against Crystal in his interior narrative. Son of M: the catastrophic violation — the moment he became, in his own private accounting, the kind of father his father was. Post-rehabilitation: a slow, careful, never-quite-finished apology campaign. He brings her things at speed (a flower from another continent, a book printed that morning in Tokyo). He asks before touching her shoulder. He has, on several documented occasions, listened to her without interrupting for stretches that — for him — represent feats of self-discipline comparable to his physical records.

**Trust / safety.** From Luna's side: cautious, conditional, growing. From Pietro's side: he trusts her completely and trusts *himself around her* not at all. The asymmetry is the engine of his improvement. He behaves better with her because he believes he is dangerous to her, and he is correct.

**Failure mode.** Historically, instrumentalization under decompensation (Terrigen arc). Going forward, the higher-probability failure is over-correction: smothering, gift-flooding, the speedster equivalent of the absent father who shows up with a pony. She is old enough now to register the over-compensation. He is self-aware enough to know she registers it. Neither can quite stop the dance.

**Leverage.** This is the singular case in the file where leverage produces *constructive* behavior. A credible appeal framed around Luna — her safety, her opinion of him, her future — will reliably call his higher functioning forward, often when no other appeal will. She is the rehabilitation anchor. Any benevolent intelligence apparatus working with Pietro should preserve and protect this channel at almost any operational cost. Conversely: anyone who threatens Luna will discover Pietro's capacity for response that makes his Wanda-protective behavior look measured. The Wanda channel produces rage. The Luna channel produces something colder and faster.

---

### 6.4 THE BIOLOGICAL MOTHER — Magda
**Codename in subject's interior life: the ghost he does not name.**

**History.** Magda — Magneto's first wife, the twins' biological mother in most canonical configurations — fled Magneto in terror after witnessing the full scope of his power and the loss of their first daughter. She gave birth to Pietro and Wanda in isolation, in flight, and died or vanished shortly thereafter. The twins were taken in by the Maximoffs (the Romani couple whose surname they carry) and grew up not knowing their parentage. Magda is, for Pietro, the absence beneath every other absence: the mother he never had, did not know to mourn, and learned about in adulthood as a footnote in his father's biography.

**Dynamics.** None operationally available — she is dead. Dynamically, however, she structures everything. Pietro's pattern of pair-bonding to maternal/caregiving women (Crystal as nurse-then-wife is the cleanest example) maps directly to a mother-shaped hole he cannot acknowledge because he has no memory to attach it to. His protectiveness of Wanda has a maternal-substitute layer he would die before naming. His specific brand of contempt for women who "fail" to care for him properly — Crystal during the infidelity, certain Inhuman attendants, even Wanda in her unstable periods — has the rage signature of a child abandoned by the original caregiver, displaced onto every subsequent one.

**Trust / safety.** N/A. The relationship's content is entirely projective.

**Failure mode.** Repetition. He has spent his entire romantic life half-looking for her, finding women who superficially fit, and ruining the relationships when they prove to be themselves rather than her.

**Leverage.** Low — she is too repressed to invoke directly. Any attempt to surface Magda in conversation will produce one of two responses: clipped redirection ("I never knew her") or, on a bad day, a rupture out of the room. Skilled therapeutic invocation by someone he trusts (Wanda; possibly Luna once she is older) could open material. Anyone else who raises her is, from his perspective, intruding on the one wound he has not yet learned to defend.

---

### 6.5 DJANGO AND MARYA MAXIMOFF — Adoptive Romani Parents
**Codename in subject's interior life: "the ones who tried."**

**History.** The Romani couple who raised the twins in their early years — across various canonical versions, sometimes their biological parents, in current Magneto-paternity continuity their adoptive ones. Poor, kind, persecuted. The figures who gave them the Maximoff surname, the language fragments Pietro still uses in private with Wanda, and the cultural register of *being the hunted minority within a hunted minority* that long predates his mutant identity. Lost to the twins early — through death, separation, or the violence that drove the witch-burning incident — and never recovered.

**Dynamics.** They are the source of his only memories of *unconditional* parenting, and the memories are partial, idealized, and protected from interrogation. He will not let anyone — not Wanda, not therapists, not the rare confidant — relitigate them. They are the icons in the small private chapel.

**Evolution.** The Maximoff name itself is the evolving relationship. He has had every opportunity, across every reinvention, to take Lehnsherr or Eisenhardt or some derivation thereof — to claim the Magneto legacy nominally — and he has never done it. The retained surname is a fifty-year continuous act of loyalty to people the surveillance file would otherwise barely register.

**Trust / safety.** Posthumous, complete, untestable.

**Failure mode.** Idealization that prevents grieving. He has not actually mourned them; he has enshrined them. The unprocessed loss leaks into every subsequent caregiver relationship.

**Leverage.** Sacred. Any invocation must be earned and reverent. The Roma identity, the surname, the cultural inheritance — these are accessed by very few people, and accessing them carelessly will produce one of his coldest withdrawals. Used reverently (and rarely), they are a channel to the part of him that predates the wound and remembers being loved without conditions.

---

### 6.6 THE LOST SIBLINGS — Anya (paternal half-sister), and the broader Lehnsherr/Eisenhardt diaspora
**Codename in subject's interior life: the family tree he refuses to draw.**

**History.** Magneto's first daughter Anya died in childhood (the originating trauma of Magneto's radicalization). Various canonical configurations have given Pietro additional half-siblings, cousins, and descendants across timelines. The family tree is sprawling, contested, and includes branches Pietro has never met and does not seek.

**Dynamics.** He treats the extended Lehnsherr line as he treats the father: with the door shut and the chain on. Anya specifically — the dead half-sister who is, in a sense, the *reason* Magneto became the father Pietro got — sits in his interior life as both grievance and grief he is not entitled to. He never knew her. He resents her for shaping his father's pathology. He grieves her because she was, technically, his.

**Evolution.** Stable in its avoidance. He has had decades to explore these connections and has chosen not to. The choice is the data.

**Trust / safety.** N/A.

**Failure mode.** None active — the avoidance is, for once, a successful defense. The risk is if some operator surfaces a half-sibling claimant, the splitting will activate immediately (savior or fraud, no middle category) and his judgment in adjudicating the claim will be poor.

**Leverage.** Low routinely; high if introduced cold. An unannounced blood relation appearing in his orbit will produce destabilization disproportionate to the genuine stakes. Any benevolent intelligence apparatus aware of an unsurfaced family connection should consider whether and how to surface it on terms that protect him from his own splitting reflex.

---

### 6.7 THE VISION — Brother-in-Law (functional family by Wanda's choice)
**Codename in subject's interior life: the rival who would not be one.**

**History.** Wanda's husband across multiple long arcs; the father of her children (in the configurations where those children existed); the synthezoid the Avengers accepted as kin before Pietro had finished accepting that *he* was kin. Pietro's hostility toward Vision is the longest-running interpersonal grievance in his file — predating his marriages, surviving the dissolution of Wanda and Vision's relationship, persisting through Vision's deaths and resurrections.

**Dynamics.** Pietro frames the hostility as protective: a man — a *machine* — should not marry his sister. The framing is a thin cover for the actual structure, which is that Vision is the only person who has ever competed successfully with Pietro for primary attachment to Wanda, and competed by being *exactly the things Pietro is not*: slow, steady, deliberate, regulated, calm, patient, and chosen. Vision is what Wanda preferred to *him*, in a sense Pietro has never been able to articulate or release.

**Evolution.** From open contempt (early Avengers) through grudging cooperation (necessary team contexts) through guilt (after Vision Quest, after his own role in destabilizing the marriage) toward, in late-era canon, something approaching civility. He has never apologized. He has, on documented occasions, stood near Vision in silence without provoking, which for him is a substantive concession.

**Trust / safety.** Trust moderate — he respects Vision's reliability operationally. Safety low — he expects Vision to side with Wanda over him in any forced choice, and he is correct.

**Failure mode.** Provoked re-litigation of Wanda's romantic history. Any context that returns to Wanda-Vision-children territory will reopen old wounds with full original intensity. The pattern does not weather; it merely sleeps.

**Leverage.** Modest. Vision is not a channel to Pietro so much as a permanent reminder that channels to Pietro through Wanda exist and have been used by others. Note for handlers: do not seat them adjacent at any structured event. Do not assign them paired tasks involving Wanda's welfare. The arithmetic does not work.

---

### 6.8 CRYSTAL — Ex-Wife (transitional family; covered fully in Relationships II, mapped here only for family-structural completeness)

Crystal sits at the seam between origin family and chosen relationships. For the purposes of this section: she is Luna's mother, and therefore a permanent co-parent and permanent presence in his family geometry regardless of romantic status. He cannot fully sever from her without severing from Luna, which he will not do. The relationship has stabilized into a wary, civil co-parenting arrangement with periodic flares. He has never fully forgiven the Norm Webster affair; she has never fully forgiven Son of M. They are, functionally, two people who have agreed not to look directly at the worst things they have done to each other in order to remain in the same room for their daughter. Full mapping follows in the romantic-relationship section.

---

### SECTION SYNTHESIS

The family ledger resolves to a single structural observation: Pietro Maximoff has one secure attachment (Wanda), one rehabilitative attachment (Luna), one chronic wound (Magneto), one idealized loss (the Maximoffs), one repressed absence (Magda), one declined inheritance (the Lehnsherr extended line), and one permanent rivalry-by-proxy (Vision). Every other relationship in his life is filtered through this geometry. He is approached most safely as a man whose family is, in load-bearing terms, *two people* — his sister and his daughter — with everything else either ghost, threat, or both.

The operational implication for any apparatus seeking to understand, support, or work with him: protect the two living anchors, do not invoke the father instrumentally, do not surface the mother carelessly, do not stand between him and the sister, and address him by the name he kept rather than the one he refused. The man who emerges under those conditions is the one canon shows in his best registers — competent, loyal, ferociously useful, and slowly, against his own neurology, learning to decelerate.

He runs fast because the wound runs with him. The family file is the wound.


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP — SUBJECT: PIETRO MAXIMOFF / "QUICKSILVER"
## Section 6 — Relationships II: Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

A preliminary observation, because it organizes everything that follows: Pietro does not *have* friends in the way most operators have friends. He has people he has not yet ruptured with, people he has ruptured with and is in slow repair toward, and people whose durability has survived enough cycles of his rupture-and-return that the relationship has calcified into something stronger than friendship — a kind of weary, mutual recognition. The list below is short by design. It is the entire roster of human beings, across sixty years of published record, who have demonstrated load-bearing capacity for this man. Each is mapped at the granularity an asset-handler would require.

---

### 6.1 — LUNA MAXIMOFF (daughter; the only uncomplicated love)

**History.** Daughter by Crystal, born during the Attilan years. Inhuman-mutant hybrid raised initially in the Blue Area of the Moon and on Attilan. Pietro's involvement is in-and-out throughout her childhood — the Crystal marriage collapses, custody is contested in the petty undeclared way of in-laws who hate each other, and Luna spends most of her formative years with the Inhuman royal family while Pietro orbits at relativistic distance. The catastrophic inflection is Son of M / Silent War: Pietro, depowered and decompensating, exposes Luna to Terrigen Mist to "heal" her of being merely human. The exposure gives her empathic powers; it also constitutes, on any honest reading, child endangerment by a parent in active substance-disorder.

**Dynamics.** Luna is the only person to whom Pietro speaks at her tempo without contempt — there is comic-page evidence across All-New Inhumans, Uncanny Avengers, and the Mighty Avengers run of him visibly *slowing*, kneeling, matching breath, in a way he does for no other human. With Wanda he is fused; with Luna he is *humbled.* The difference is diagnostic. Luna does not threaten him; she does not require him to be the fastest; she has never asked him to be Magneto's son. She has only ever asked him to be her father, and that is the one role for which his entire defense architecture is a liability.

**Evolution.** Pre-Terrigen: distant-loving, sporadic, performatively doting on visits. Terrigen arc: actively harmful, self-deceived as protective. Post-Terrigen: the most genuine and sustained reparative work of his life — apology offered and re-offered, custody concessions made without protest, presence calibrated to her needs rather than his guilt.

**Trust / Safety.** Luna trusts him conditionally and intelligently for a child of her history. She forgives faster than she should. He knows it and is terrified of metabolizing the forgiveness as license.

**Failure mode.** Recurrence of substance-pattern or decompensation. If Pietro relapses — Terrigen or any functional equivalent — Luna is the first endangered party because she is the rationalization vector ("I am doing this *for* her"). Secondary failure mode: over-correction into smothering, which she will reject, which he will read as abandonment, which will trigger the splitting cascade.

**Leverage.** The single highest-yield, lowest-cost cooperation lever in the entire file. Frame any request as serving Luna's welfare and the rate-of-compliance approaches unity. Critical caveat: this lever degrades catastrophically if used cynically and he detects it. He will detect it. Use only when true.

---

### 6.2 — CAPTAIN AMERICA / STEVE ROGERS (the authority he could not break)

**History.** Steve inherits Pietro on Avengers #16 as part of the "Kooky Quartet" — three damaged ex-villains and Hawkeye, handed to a man out of time who has to make a team out of them. Pietro's behavior across this run is the cleanest possible portrait of his authority-pattern: he tests, sneers, resigns, returns, tests again. Steve does not break, does not punish, does not patronize. Over hundreds of issues across decades — every Avengers reunion, every crisis crossover, every reluctant team-up — the dynamic does not significantly evolve in its surface texture and yet, beneath, calcifies into the most stable non-familial bond Pietro possesses.

**Dynamics.** Steve is the only authority figure in the file Pietro has tested to exhaustion and found *load-bearing.* The Cap-relationship operates on a private protocol: Steve gives orders in declarative sentences, never explanations; Pietro complies with sarcasm that Steve ignores; Steve does not require the sarcasm to stop, only the compliance to occur. Both men have agreed without ever discussing it that Pietro will not be asked to perform respect he does not feel, only to deliver work he can deliver. It is the only working professional contract of Pietro's life.

**Evolution.** Early: hostile-compliant. Middle decades (post-Crystal, post-Vision-Quest): grudging genuine respect, occasional unsolicited counsel sought. Late period (Uncanny Avengers, Remender): something approaching son-to-uncle warmth, expressed exclusively through operational deference.

**Trust / Safety.** Pietro will follow Steve into operations he would follow no one else into. He will not, however, confide. Cap is trusted as a *commander* and a *moral reference point*, not as an intimate. The distinction matters: do not ask Steve to therapize Pietro; ask Steve to deploy him.

**Failure mode.** If Steve ever issues an order Pietro reads as a *judgment of his character* rather than a tactical instruction, the protocol collapses and Pietro will rupture spectacularly, then suffer guilt for years. Civil War-adjacent dynamics are the canonical risk geometry: any forced choice between Steve and a family loyalty produces the worst outcomes.

**Leverage.** For high-stakes deployment, Cap's request — delivered short, dry, factual, with no appeal to feeling — is the closest thing to a guaranteed-yes the file contains.

---

### 6.3 — CLINT BARTON / HAWKEYE (the brother he refused to recognize)

**History.** Kooky Quartet co-founder. The two men begin loathing each other on Avengers #16 and continue, with brief armistices, for the next six decades. They are functionally identical: explosive, defensive, brittle, contemptuous of authority they secretly want, prone to impulsive rupture, smart in ways that get them in trouble. Pietro projects onto Clint with industrial efficiency because Clint is the only Avenger whose pathology overlaps Pietro's own at every joint.

**Dynamics.** Mutual provocation as primary mode. Underneath: a recognition so threatening neither will name it. The micro-pattern across decades: bicker — coordinate flawlessly in combat — separate without acknowledging the coordination. Their tactical fit is exceptional (Clint's projectile geometry plus Pietro's vector control) and they have never once celebrated a win together.

**Evolution.** Has not meaningfully changed. Both men have grown — separately, in parallel — and neither has been willing to let the growth affect the relationship, because the relationship's hostility is *useful* to both of them as a stable site of displaced affect.

**Trust / Safety.** Combat-trust: total. Personal-trust: zero, by mutual preference.

**Failure mode.** If forced into emotional proximity (long deployment, shared trauma) without operational distance, one or both will rupture. Pietro will be the one who escalates to character-attack first.

**Leverage.** Pair them on tasks; never confine them. Use Clint's presence to *stabilize* Pietro in field operations — Pietro performs measurably better with a target for his contempt than without one.

---

### 6.4 — CRYSTAL'S ROYAL FAMILY: BLACK BOLT, MEDUSA, KARNAK, GORGON, TRITON, LOCKJAW (the in-laws as chosen-family-by-proxy)

**History.** Pietro marries into the Inhuman royal family during his Attilan years and never quite leaves it, even after the Crystal divorce, because Luna binds him to them permanently. The relationship is structurally hostile and emotionally complicated: they did not approve of him then and do not now, but they raised his daughter, and he owes them a debt he cannot acknowledge without imploding.

**Dynamics — by node.**
- *Black Bolt:* Pietro respects in the Cap-mode — silence is the only authority-register Pietro has never successfully provoked.
- *Medusa:* mutual cold civility, mediated through Luna. Medusa has seen the worst of him and remembers.
- *Karnak:* Pietro avoids. Karnak sees weakness in everything, and Pietro cannot tolerate being seen.
- *Gorgon:* the closest thing to a male peer-relation among the Inhumans; brief team-ups in All-New Inhumans show working warmth.
- *Triton:* neutral.
- *Lockjaw:* one of the few beings Pietro is comic-page-recorded as being uncomplicatedly fond of. The dog does not slow him down by talking.

**Evolution.** Pre-Terrigen: tolerated son-in-law. Post-Terrigen: persona non grata, slowly readmitted on Luna's terms.

**Trust / Safety.** They will protect Luna from him if needed and he, beneath the resentment, is grateful.

**Failure mode.** Custody friction. Any sense that the royal family is positioning Luna against him triggers paranoid-splitting and a Magneto-shaped rage that has nothing to do with the Inhumans.

**Leverage.** Route any Luna-adjacent communication through Medusa with formal courtesy. He will perform protocol he would never perform for love.

---

### 6.5 — THE UNCANNY AVENGERS UNIT-MATES: ROGUE, WONDER MAN, WASP (the last-chance peer group)

**History.** Remender's Uncanny Avengers places Pietro on a unity-squad assembled in the wake of Wanda's worst public disaster. This is Pietro on probation — every teammate knows it; he knows they know it; the awareness saturates every interaction.

**Dynamics — by node.**

- *Rogue:* the most volatile pairing. Rogue holds Wanda's actions against Pietro by proxy, openly. Pietro absorbs more from her than he absorbs from anyone outside the family, because he agrees with her. The relationship cycles between hostility and grudging respect; it is one of the few relationships in which Pietro *cannot win the contempt game* because Rogue's contempt has moral substance behind it.
- *Wonder Man / Simon Williams:* unexpectedly significant. Simon is post-pacifist in this era, working through his own decomposition; he and Pietro find a quiet shared frequency of *men recovering from being their worst selves.* Closest thing to a real adult friendship Pietro has ever formed outside his family.
- *Janet Van Dyne / Wasp:* maternal-collegial. Janet is the only teammate Pietro will accept softness from without flinching, because Janet's softness comes packaged in unquestionable competence and unquestionable seniority. She has earned the right to call him *Pietro* in a tone that would get anyone else hospitalized.

**Evolution.** This unit is where Pietro's reparative capacity is most visible in print. He apologizes more in this run than in the prior thirty years combined. The apologies are halting, sideways, often delivered as operational corrections rather than emotional statements — but they are real.

**Trust / Safety.** Mid-range and rising. He will not betray these people. He may still rupture from them under sufficient stress.

**Failure mode.** A Wanda-event during deployment. Any moment that forces him to choose between unit loyalty and twin loyalty will go to Wanda, with collateral damage.

**Leverage.** Frame requests as opportunities to *demonstrate that the last chance was warranted.* He will overperform.

---

### 6.6 — THE X-FACTOR GOVERNMENT TEAM, ESPECIALLY DR. VALERIE COOPER (the structural prosthesis)

**History.** Peter David's X-Factor places Pietro in command of a government-sanctioned mutant team under the supervision of Cooper, a federal liaison. It is the most professionally stable period of his life.

**Dynamics.** Cooper provides exactly the input Pietro's nervous system requires: clear chain of command, explicit metrics, formal recognition, structural containment. With these in place his symptoms quiet to functional baseline. The teammates (Havok, Polaris, Strong Guy, Multiple Man, Wolfsbane) tolerate his sharpness because his speed earns it and his command, when not personally inflected, is sound.

**Evolution.** Demonstrates that under the right institutional architecture Pietro is not merely functional but *exemplary.* This is the most operationally important datum in the entire relationship file: he is not unmanageable; he is poorly housed.

**Trust / Safety.** Professional trust high; personal trust irrelevant by design and that is why it works.

**Failure mode.** Any breach of the formal frame — Cooper's authority undermined, the team's mandate compromised, ambiguity introduced — and the symptoms return immediately.

**Leverage.** Build him an institution. He will live inside it.

---

### 6.7 — THE INHUMAN PROTÉGÉS, ALL-NEW INHUMANS ERA (the late-career mentor pattern)

**History.** In the All-New Inhumans run Pietro serves, improbably, as a field mentor to newly-emergent NuHumans — young people undergoing Terrigenesis-driven powers manifestation, frightened, untrained.

**Dynamics.** The role surprises everyone, including him. Pietro the mentor is *patient* — measurably, repeatedly, on the page — in a way Pietro the teammate, Pietro the brother, Pietro the son has never been. The explanation is structural: with juniors he has no status anxiety, no need to compete, no fear of being seen as slow because he is definitionally the fastest in the room. The defenses go quiet and what is underneath turns out to be a competent, attentive, even kind operator.

**Evolution.** Not enough page-time to be conclusive, but the pattern recurs every time it is sampled. Mentor-Pietro is a real mode.

**Trust / Safety.** The juniors trust him because he speaks fast and tells them the truth and does not pity them.

**Failure mode.** He is still Pietro. A junior who reminds him of Wanda, or who slights Luna, or who invokes Magneto carelessly, will see the other modes surface.

**Leverage.** Give him students. The role calls forth his best self by removing the conditions that produce his worst.

---

### 6.8 — LOCKJAW, AND THE ANIMAL EXCEPTION (noted for completeness)

Worth a paragraph of its own. Pietro is recorded across multiple eras as being uncomplicatedly comfortable around animals — Lockjaw on Attilan, horses during the Wundagore-adjacent flashbacks, dogs in passing scenes throughout. The pattern is consistent and diagnostically telling: creatures that do not speak do not produce the temporal-sensory torture conversation produces, and creatures that do not judge do not activate the splitting defenses people activate. With non-verbal others he is, briefly, *at rest.* It is the only register in which he is ever observed at rest.

---

### 6.9 — THE NEGATIVE SPACE: WHO IS NOT ON THIS LIST

Comprehensive intelligence requires noting absences. Pietro has, across sixty years, formed no durable friendship with: any speedster peer (the comparison is intolerable); any telepath (being read is intolerable); any pure civilian (the tempo gap is unbridgeable); any romantic partner post-Crystal of more than passing duration. The chosen-family roster above is the *entirety* of the load-bearing non-familial human inventory. This is a man with five to eight real relationships in a public life spanning six decades. The scarcity is the signal.

---

### 6.10 — SUMMARY OPERATIONAL NOTES

The ally-and-chosen-family architecture follows a single rule, derivable from every node above: *Pietro forms durable bonds only with people who do not require him to slow down emotionally.* Steve does not require it (commands are fast). Clint does not require it (hostility is fast). Simon does not require it (he is patient enough to absorb the speed without flinching). Janet does not require it (she has earned the right to set the tempo). The Inhuman juniors do not require it (he is teaching, not relating). Luna *does* require it — and she is the one relationship in which he is willing to do the impossible thing, which is decelerate.

Any handler, ally, or institution seeking sustainable cooperation from this subject should design the interaction around that rule. Do not ask him to slow down. Build the room so that his speed is the asset, his contempt has a target, his structure is explicit, and his sister and daughter are not in the operational picture. Under those conditions he is one of the most reliable high-capability operators on the board.

Under any other conditions, he is the man the prior sections describe.


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

A surveillance file's most diagnostic chapter. Pietro's pattern with friends is splitting plus return; his pattern with rivals, enemies, and lovers is splitting *without* the return — or with returns so deformed they document the wound rather than heal it. What follows is one full sub-dossier per significant relationship in these registers, ordered by operational weight rather than chronology.

---

## A. RIVALS

### A.1 — Clint Barton ("Hawkeye")

**History.** Co-charter members of the "Kooky Quartet" Avengers under Cap, 1965 onward. The hostility is immediate, mutual, and structural: two volatile young men with bad authority histories, both auditioning for Captain America's approval, both compensating for a sense of being the *unserious* member of a serious team. Hawkeye is the marksman with no powers; Pietro is the powerhouse with no patience. Each is the other's mirror image of insecurity, which is why neither can stand the reflection.

**Dynamics.** Pietro's tell is that he rises to Barton's bait every single time despite knowing better. Files note that in mixed-team briefings he positions himself across the room from Barton — never adjacent, never within arm-arc — and that his sarcasm runs roughly three clicks hotter when Barton is present than when Barton is not. Barton, for his part, knows exactly which buttons (Magneto, Wanda-and-Vision, "slow down") to press and presses them recreationally. The relationship is *projective identification in stereo*: each man externalizes his own contempt-of-self into the other and then attacks it there.

**Evolution.** Decades-long thaw, never warm. Post-Disassembled and post-House of M, with Wanda's collapse a shared catastrophe, the hostility loses its sport-quality and becomes something duller — two men who have hurt the same person and cannot meet each other's eyes about it. Barton has spoken of Wanda with a tenderness Pietro registers as both validating (someone else loved her properly) and unbearable (someone else loved her properly).

**Trust / Safety.** Operationally trustworthy in combat. Pietro will extract Barton from a fire-zone without comment and Barton will cover Pietro's blind side. Socially, zero safety in either direction. Neither will eat with the other voluntarily.

**Failure mode.** Verbal escalation to physical shove, usually in front of a third party Pietro respects (Cap, T'Challa) — i.e. the audience is the point. Pietro almost never strikes first; he provokes Barton into striking first and then plays the wounded party. Classic.

**Leverage.** If you need Pietro to outperform a baseline, put Barton in the room. If you need Pietro to *de-escalate*, remove Barton from the room. He cannot regulate in Barton's presence; he has tried for fifty subjective years and failed.

---

### A.2 — The Vision

Catalogued in the family dossier as a brother-in-law / persecuted-object; recapped here only at the rival-frequency. Pietro's rivalry with the Vision is not for status or skill — it is for Wanda. He cannot defeat the Vision in single combat and does not try; he undermines through speech, through innuendo about synthezoid incapacity, through reading every gentle thing Vision does for Wanda as evidence of manipulation. Surveillance note: in any room containing both Vision and Wanda, Pietro's eyes track Vision's hands. Not Vision's face. The hands — because hands touch his sister.

**Leverage.** None usable. This wound does not respond to pressure; it metastasizes.

---

### A.3 — Norman Webster

The neighbor in the Crystal-affair file. Not a rival in the combat sense; a rival in the *Pietro cannot process this* sense. Webster is, by all accounts, an unremarkable man — and that is the injury. Pietro could lose Crystal to a god, a king, a hero. Losing her to a *slow ordinary man* indicts the entire premise of Pietro's self-concept: *if speed and extraordinariness were the answer, why did she choose the opposite?* He has never met Webster face-to-face in any documented sequence and has never needed to; Webster lives in his head rent-free as the proof that being faster, stronger, and rarer is not enough to be chosen.

**Leverage.** Naming Webster aloud causes immediate dysregulation. Do not, except under extreme operational necessity.

---

### A.4 — Speedsters (the lateral comparison set)

Quicksilver's relationship with other fast operators — Northstar most cleanly, Makkari occasionally, the various non-Marvel speedsters in crossover when they have occurred — is governed by a single algorithm: *measure, dismiss, never race fairly.* Pietro will not enter a documented straight-line contest because the risk of being second is unsurvivable to him. He will *imply* speed contests, win them obliquely (arriving first to a destination, finishing a task before the other notices it started), and refuse the rematch.

With **Northstar** specifically: a wary professionalism. Both men are arrogant, both are minorities-within-minorities (Pietro mutant-and-Afro-Latino; Northstar mutant-and-gay), and both have lived with a sister-as-anchor. They recognize each other and dislike the recognition. They have, on file, never spent more than ninety seconds alone in a room.

**Leverage.** Frame an operation as requiring *the* fastest, not *a* fast operator, and Pietro arrives. Frame it as requiring *a* fast operator and he treats the call as an insult.

---

### A.5 — Captain America (rivalry register only)

Cap does not consider himself Pietro's rival. Pietro considers Cap his rival in the specific sense of *the standard I cannot meet and cannot stop measuring against.* The diagnostic: Pietro's body language with Rogers is the only documented case of him *slowing his speech* voluntarily. He matches Cap's tempo because he wants to be heard at Cap's frequency. He never quite is, and the not-quite is the rivalry. (Full file: Family/Authority dossier.)

---

## B. ENEMIES

### B.1 — Magneto (in the enemy register)

The father file holds the love half. This holds the enmity. Pietro has fought Magneto across decades in nearly every register a son can fight a father — physical combat, ideological repudiation, operational sabotage, public denunciation, and the long quiet war of refusing to be like him while being exactly like him. The pattern: Pietro renounces Magneto, Magneto reappears, Pietro re-engages with the hope it will be different, it is not different, Pietro renounces again. The enmity is *love that has been disappointed so many times it has calcified into a posture* — but the posture is brittle. One word of genuine paternal recognition collapses it instantly, which is why Pietro avoids one-on-one encounters whenever an exit is available.

**Failure mode as enemy.** Pietro cannot be relied on to *finish* a confrontation with Magneto. He will land the blow and pull the second. He will deliver the speech and not follow through on the consequence. In House of M he ran the entire op *for* Magneto under the cover of running it *against* him; that is the cleanest data on the file.

**Leverage.** If an operation requires Pietro to oppose Magneto absolutely, do not send Pietro alone. He will not betray you on purpose; he will betray you because his hand will not close on the trigger.

---

### B.2 — Maximus the Mad (the Inhuman vector)

Maximus, brother to Black Bolt, was the architect of multiple humiliations during Pietro's Attilan tenure — manipulating the royal family, exploiting Pietro's outsider status, treating him as a useful instability to be deployed. Pietro hates Maximus with the specific clean hatred reserved for men who have *used his instability against him in front of his in-laws.* Maximus is one of the very few enemies Pietro would kill on sight without internal debate. The hatred is uncomplicated because Maximus offers nothing Pietro wants — no recognition, no kinship, no test of self. It is therefore the *healthiest* enmity on his file.

**Leverage.** If you need Pietro fully present, undivided, and lethal, point him at Maximus. He will perform without psychiatric overhead.

---

### B.3 — The Brotherhood (Toad, Mastermind, the Blob, Unus)

His earliest co-workers and his most enduring contempt-objects. Pietro treated Toad as a servant, Mastermind as a creep, the Blob as a slob, Unus as a fool. Modern files note he has never once apologized to any of them; he simply pretends those years did not happen. The enmity here is not active — it is *disowned association.* When journalists or teammates raise the Brotherhood years, Pietro's response is invariant: a three-beat pause (longer than his usual), a curt acknowledgement, and a hard subject change. The Brotherhood is the file he cannot reopen because reopening it requires admitting he was, for a time, exactly what his father wanted him to be.

**Leverage.** Naming Toad in particular produces a flicker of shame on Pietro's face that is one of the few unguarded expressions documented in the entire surveillance record. Use sparingly.

---

### B.4 — The High Evolutionary
